Page 1
India 
Coordinates: [URL: "https://geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=India&params=21_N_78_E_region:IN_type:country_source:dewiki"] 21°N 78°E
India,  officially the Republic of India (Hindi: Bhārat
Gaṇarājya),[26] is a country in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Asia"] South Asia. It is the
 seventh-largest country by area, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population"] second-most populous
country, and the most populous [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democracy"] democracy in the world.
 Bounded by the Indian Ocean on the south, the Arabian
Sea on the southwest, and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bay_of_Bengal"] Bay of Bengal on the
southeast, it shares land borders with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistan"] Pakistan to the
west;[f] China, Nepal, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bhutan"] Bhutan to the north; and
 Bangladesh and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Myanmar"] Myanmar to the east. In the Indian Ocean,
India is in the vicinity of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sri_Lanka"] Sri Lanka and the Maldives; its
 Andaman and Nicobar Islands share a maritime border
with Thailand, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Myanmar"] Myanmar and Indonesia.
 Modern humans arrived on the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_subcontinent"] Indian subcontinent from
Africa no later than 55,000 years ago.[27][28][29]Their
long occupation, initially in varying forms of isolation as
hunter-gatherers, has made the region highly diverse,
second only to Africa in human [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetic_diversity"] genetic diversity.[30]
 Settled life emerged on the subcontinent in the western
margins of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indus_River"] Indus [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/River_basin"] river basin 9,000 years ago, evolving
gradually into the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indus_Valley_Civilisation"] Indus Valley Civilisation of the third
millennium BCE.[31]By 1200 BCE, an [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proto-language"] archaic form of
Sanskrit, an [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-European_language"] Indo-European language, had [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trans-cultural_diffusion"] diffused into
India from the northwest,[32][33] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oral_transmission"] unfolding as the language
of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rigveda"] Rigveda, and recording the dawning of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hinduism"] Hinduism in
India.[34] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dravidian_languages"] Dravidian languages of India were
supplanted in the northern and western regions.[35]By
400 BCE, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_stratification"] stratification and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_exclusion"] exclusion by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caste"] caste had
emerged within Hinduism,[36]and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Buddhism_in_India"] Buddhism and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Jainism"] Jainism
had arisen, proclaiming [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_order"] social orders unlinked to
heredity.[37]Early political consolidations gave rise to the
 loose-knit Maurya and Gupta Empires based in the Ganges
Basin.[38]Their collective [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Era"] era was suffused with wide-
ranging creativity,[39] but also marked by the declining
status of women,[40] and the incorporation of
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Untouchability"] untouchability into an organised system of belief.[g][41] In
 South India, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_kingdoms_of_India#The_Deccan_plateau_and_South"] Middle kingdoms exported Dravidian-
languages scripts and religious cultures to the kingdoms of
 Southeast Asia.[42]
In the early medieval era, Christianity, Islam, Judaism, and
 Zoroastrianism became established on India's southern and
western coasts.[43]Muslim armies from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Asia"] Central Asia
intermittently overran India's northern plains,[44]eventually
founding the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Delhi_Sultanate"] Delhi Sultanate, and drawing northern India 
Republic of India
Bhārat Gaṇarājya

Page 2
into the cosmopolitan [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age"] networks of medieval Islam.[45]In
the 15th century, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vijayanagara_Empire"] Vijayanagara Empire created a long-
lasting composite Hindu culture in south India.[46]In the
Punjab, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sikhism"] Sikhism emerged, rejecting institutionalised
religion.[47]The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mughal_Empire"] Mughal Empire, in 1526, ushered in two
centuries of relative peace,[48]leaving a legacy of
 luminous architecture.[h][49]Gradually expanding rule of
the British East India Company followed, turning India
into a colonial economy, but also consolidating its
sovereignty.[50] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Raj"] British Crown rule began in 1858. The
rights promised to Indians were granted slowly,[51][52] but
 technological changes were introduced, and ideas of
education, modernity and the public life took root.[53] A
pioneering and influential nationalist movement emerged,
which was noted for nonviolent resistance and became the
major factor in ending British rule.[54][55] In 1947 the
British Indian Empire was [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Partition_of_India"] partitioned into two independent
 dominions,[56][57][58][59] a Hindu-majority Dominion of
India and a Muslim-majority [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dominion_of_Pakistan"] Dominion of Pakistan, amid
large-scale loss of life and an unprecedented migration.[60]
India has been a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_republic"] federal republic since 1950, governed in a
democratic [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parliamentary_system"] parliamentary system. It is a pluralistic,
 multilingual and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multiculturalism"] multi-ethnic society. India's population
grew from 361 million in 1951 to 1.211 billion in 2011.[61]
During the same time, its nominal [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Per_capita_income"] per capita income
increased from US$64 annually to US$1,498, and its
literacy rate from 16.6% to 74%.  From being a
comparatively destitute country in 1951,[62]India has
become a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_real_GDP_growth_rate"] fast-growing [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G20"] major economy and a hub for
 information technology services, with an expanding middle
class.[63] It has [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_Space_Research_Organisation"] a space programme which includes several
planned or completed [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Solar_System_probes"] extraterrestrial missions. Indian
movies, music, and spiritual teachings play an increasing
role in global culture.[64]India has substantially reduced its
rate of poverty, though at the cost of increasing economic
inequality.[65]India is a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_states_with_nuclear_weapons"] nuclear-weapon state, which ranks
high in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_military_expenditures"] military expenditure. It has disputes over [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kashmir"] Kashmir
with its neighbours, Pakistan and China, unresolved since
the mid-20th century.[66]Among the socio-economic
 challenges India faces are gender inequality, child
malnutrition,[67]and rising levels of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Air_pollution_in_India"] air pollution.[68]
 India's  land is megadiverse, with four biodiversity
hotspots.[69] Its forest cover comprises 21.7% of its
area.[70] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wildlife_in_India"] India's wildlife, which has traditionally been
viewed with tolerance in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Culture_of_India"] India's culture,[71] is supported
among these forests, and elsewhere, in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protected_areas_of_India"] protected habitats.

Etymology
According to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxford_English_Dictionary"] Oxford English Dictionary (third edition 2009), the name "India" is derived from the
 Classical Latin India, a reference to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Asia"] South Asia and an uncertain region to its east; and in turn derived
successively from: [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hellenistic_Greek"] Hellenistic Greek India ( Ἰνδία); [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greek"] ancient Greek Indos ( Ἰνδός); [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Persian"] Old Persian [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindush"] Hindush, an
eastern province of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Achaemenid_empire"] Achaemenid empire; and ultimately its cognate, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanskrit"] Sanskrit Sindhu, or "river,"
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/.in#Internationalised_domain_names_and_country_codes"]
Page 4
specifically the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indus_River"] Indus River and, by implication, its well-settled southern basin.[72][73] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greece"] ancient Greeks
 referred to the Indians as Indoi (Ἰνδοί (https://www.loc.gov/standards/iso639-2/php/langcodes_name.php?c
ode_ID=)), which translates as "The people of the Indus".[74]
The term [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Names_for_India#Bh%C4%81rata"] Bharat (Bhārat; pronounced  [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA/Hindi_and_Urdu"] [ˈbʱaːɾət] (  listen)), mentioned in both [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_epic_poetry"] Indian epic poetry and the
 Constitution of India,[75][76] is used in its variations by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Names_of_India_in_its_official_languages"] many Indian languages. A modern rendering of the
historical name Bharatavarsha, which applied originally to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_India"] North India,[77][78] Bharat gained increased
currency from the mid-19th century as a native name for India.[75][79]
 Hindustan ([ɦɪndʊˈstaːn] (  listen)) is a Middle Persian name for India, introduced during the Mughal
Empire and used widely since. Its meaning has varied, referring to a region encompassing present-day
northern India and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistan"] Pakistan or to India in its near entirety.[75][79][80]
History
Ancient India
By 55,000 years ago, the first modern humans, or [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homo_sapiens"] Homo sapiens,
had arrived on the Indian subcontinent from Africa, where they had
earlier evolved.[27][28][29] The earliest known modern human
remains in South Asia date to about 30,000 years ago.[27] After
6500 BCE, evidence for domestication of food crops and animals,
construction of permanent structures, and storage of agricultural
surplus appeared in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mehrgarh"] Mehrgarh and other sites in what is now
 Balochistan, Pakistan.[82] These gradually developed into the Indus
Valley Civilisation,[83][82] the first urban culture in South Asia,[84]
which flourished during 2500–1900 BCE in what is now Pakistan
and western India.[85] Centred around cities such as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohenjo-daro"] Mohenjo-daro, 
An illustration from an early-modern
manuscript of the Sanskrit epic
Ramayana, composed in story-telling
fashion c. 400 BCE – c. 300 CE.[81]
Harappa, Dholavira, and Kalibangan, and relying on varied forms
of subsistence, the civilisation engaged robustly in crafts production and wide-ranging trade.[84]
During the period 2000–500 BCE, many regions of the subcontinent transitioned from the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chalcolithic"] Chalcolithic
cultures to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iron_Age"] Iron Age ones.[86] The Vedas, the oldest scriptures associated with Hinduism,[87] were
 composed during this period,[88] and historians have analysed these to posit a Vedic culture in the Punjab
region and the upper [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Gangetic_Plain"] Gangetic Plain.[86] Most historians also consider this period to have encompassed
several waves of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Aryan_migration"] Indo-Aryan migration into the subcontinent from the north-west.[87] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caste_system"] caste system,
which created a hierarchy of priests, warriors, and free peasants, but which excluded indigenous peoples by
labelling their occupations impure, arose during this period.[89] On the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deccan_Plateau"] Deccan Plateau, archaeological
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_India"] evidence from this period suggests the existence of a chiefdom stage of political organisation.[86] In South
India, a progression to sedentary life is indicated by the large number of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Megalith"] megalithic monuments dating from
this period,[90] as well as by nearby traces of agriculture, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Irrigation_tanks"] irrigation tanks, and craft traditions.[90]
In the late Vedic period, around the 6th century BCE, the small states and chiefdoms of the Ganges Plain
and the north-western regions had consolidated into 16 major oligarchies and monarchies that were known
as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahajanapadas"] mahajanapadas.[91][92] The emerging urbanisation gave rise to non-Vedic religious movements, two
of which became independent religions. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jainism"] Jainism came into prominence during the life of its exemplar,
Mahavira.[93] Buddhism, based on the teachings of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gautama_Buddha"] Gautama Buddha, attracted followers from all social
classes excepting the middle class; chronicling the life of the Buddha was central to the beginnings of
recorded history in India.[94][95][96] In an age of increasing urban wealth, both religions held up
 renunciation as an ideal,[97] and both established long-lasting monastic traditions. Politically, by the 3rd
Page 5
century BCE, the kingdom of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magadha"] Magadha had annexed or reduced
other states to emerge as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maurya_Empire"] Mauryan Empire.[98] The empire was
once thought to have controlled most of the subcontinent except the
far south, but its core regions are now thought to have been
separated by large autonomous areas.[99][100] The Mauryan kings
are known as much for their empire-building and determined
management of public life as for [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ashoka"] Ashoka's renunciation of
militarism and far-flung advocacy of the Buddhist
 dhamma.[101][102]  [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ajanta_Caves"] Cave 26 of the rock-cut Ajanta
Caves
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sangam_literature"] Sangam literature of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tamil_language"] Tamil language reveals that, between
200 BCE and 200 CE, the southern peninsula was ruled by the
Cheras, the Cholas, and the Pandyas, dynasties that [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Roman_trade"] traded extensively with the Roman Empire and with
 West and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southeast_Asia"] South-East Asia.[103][104] In North India, Hinduism asserted patriarchal control within the family,
leading to increased subordination of women.[105][98] By the 4th and 5th centuries, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gupta_Empire"] Gupta Empire had
created a complex system of administration and taxation in the greater Ganges Plain; this system became a
model for later Indian kingdoms.[106][107] Under the Guptas, a renewed Hinduism based on devotion,
rather than the management of ritual, began to assert itself.[108] This renewal was reflected in a flowering of
 sculpture and architecture, which found patrons among an urban elite.[107] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanskrit_literature#Classical_Sanskrit_literature"] Classical Sanskrit literature
flowered as well, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_science_and_technology_in_the_Indian_subcontinent"] Indian science, astronomy, medicine, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_mathematics"] mathematics made significant
advances.[107]
Medieval India 
The Indian early medieval age, from 600 to
1200 CE, is defined by regional kingdoms and
cultural diversity.[109] When [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harsha"] Harsha of Kannauj,
who ruled much of the Indo-Gangetic Plain from 606
to 647 CE, attempted to expand southwards, he was
defeated by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chalukya_dynasty"] Chalukya ruler of the Deccan.[110]
When his successor attempted to expand eastwards,
he was defeated by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pala_Empire"] Pala king of Bengal.[110]
When the Chalukyas attempted to expand
southwards, they were defeated by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pallava_dynasty"] Pallavas from
 Brihadeshwara temple,
Thanjavur, completed in
1010 CE 
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qutub_Minar"] Qutub Minar, 73 m
(240 ft) tall, completed by
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sultan_of_Delhi"] Sultan of Delhi,
 Iltutmish 
farther south, who in turn were opposed by the
 Pandyas and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chola_dynasty"] Cholas from still farther south.[110]
No ruler of this period was able to create an empire
and consistently control lands much beyond their
core region.[109] During this time, pastoral peoples,
whose land had been cleared to make way for the
growing agricultural economy, were accommodated
within caste society, as were new non-traditional ruling classes.[111] The caste system consequently began
to show regional differences.[111]
In the 6th and 7th centuries, the first [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bhakti"] devotional hymns were created in the Tamil language.[112] They were
 imitated all over India and led to both the resurgence of Hinduism and the development of all modern
languages of the subcontinent.[112] Indian royalty, big and small, and the temples they patronised drew
citizens in great numbers to the capital cities, which became economic hubs as well.[113] Temple towns of
various sizes began to appear everywhere as India underwent another urbanisation.[113] By the 8th and 9th
centuries, the effects were felt in South-East Asia, as South Indian culture and political systems were
Page 6
exported to lands that became part of modern-day Myanmar, Thailand, Laos, Brunei, Cambodia, Vietnam,
Philippines, Malaysia, and Indonesia.[114] Indian merchants, scholars, and sometimes armies were involved
in this transmission; South-East Asians took the initiative as well, with many sojourning in Indian
seminaries and translating Buddhist and Hindu texts into their languages.[114]
After the 10th century, Muslim Central Asian nomadic clans, using [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Courser_(horse)"] swift-horse cavalry and raising vast
armies united by ethnicity and religion, repeatedly overran South Asia's north-western plains, leading
eventually to the establishment of the Islamic [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Delhi_Sultanate"] Delhi Sultanate in 1206.[115] The sultanate was to control
much of North India and to make many forays into South India. Although at first disruptive for the Indian
elites, the sultanate largely left its vast non-Muslim subject population to its own laws and
customs.[116][117] By repeatedly repulsing [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mongol_Empire"] Mongol raiders in the 13th century, the sultanate saved India
from the devastation visited on West and Central Asia, setting the scene for centuries of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_migration"] migration of fleeing
soldiers, learned men, mystics, traders, artists, and artisans from that region into the subcontinent, thereby
creating a syncretic Indo-Islamic culture in the north.[118][119] The sultanate's raiding and weakening of the
regional kingdoms of South India paved the way for the indigenous [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vijayanagara_Empire"] Vijayanagara Empire.[120] Embracing
a strong [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shaivism"] Shaivite tradition and building upon the military technology of the sultanate, the empire came to
control much of peninsular India,[121] and was to influence South Indian society for long afterwards.[120]
Early modern India
In the early 16th century, northern India, then under mainly Muslim rulers,[122] fell again to the superior
mobility and firepower of a new generation of Central Asian warriors.[123] The resulting Mughal Empire
did not stamp out the local societies it came to rule. Instead, it balanced and pacified them through new
administrative practices[124][125] and diverse and inclusive ruling elites,[126] leading to more systematic,
centralised, and uniform rule.[127] Eschewing tribal bonds and Islamic identity, especially under Akbar, the
Mughals united their far-flung realms through loyalty, expressed through a Persianised culture, to an
emperor who had near-divine status.[126] The Mughal state's economic policies, deriving most revenues
from agriculture[128] and mandating that taxes be paid in the well-regulated silver currency,[129] caused
peasants and artisans to enter larger markets.[127] The relative peace maintained by the empire during much
of the 17th century was a factor in India's economic expansion,[127] resulting in greater patronage of
painting, literary forms, textiles, and architecture.[130] Newly coherent social groups in northern and
western India, such as the Marathas, the Rajputs, and the Sikhs, gained military and governing ambitions
during Mughal rule, which, through collaboration or adversity, gave them both recognition and military
experience.[131] Expanding commerce during Mughal rule gave rise to new Indian commercial and
political elites along the coasts of southern and eastern India.[131] As the empire disintegrated, many among
these elites were able to seek and control their own affairs.[132]
By the early 18th century, with the lines
between commercial and political dominance
being increasingly blurred, a number of
European trading companies, including the
English [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_India_Company"] East India Company, had established
coastal outposts.[133][134] The East India
Company's  control of the seas, greater
resources, and more advanced military training
and technology led it to increasingly assert its
military strength and caused it to become 
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taj_Mahal"] A distant view of the Taj A two [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohur"] mohur Company gold
Mahal from the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agra_Fort"] Agra Fort coin, issued in 1835, the
 obverse inscribed "William IV,
King"
attractive to a portion of the Indian elite; these
factors were crucial in allowing the company
to gain control over the Bengal region by 1765 and sideline the other European
Page 7
companies.[135][133][136][137] Its further access to the riches of Bengal and the subsequent increased
strength and size of its army enabled it to annexe or subdue most of India by the 1820s.[138] India was then
no longer exporting manufactured goods as it long had, but was instead supplying the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Empire"] British Empire with
raw materials. Many historians consider this to be the onset of India's colonial period.[133] By this time,
with its economic power severely curtailed by the British parliament and having effectively been made an
arm of British administration, the company began more consciously to enter non-economic arenas,
including education, social reform and culture.[139]
Modern India
Historians consider India's modern age to have begun sometime between 1848 and 1885. The appointment
in 1848 of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Broun-Ramsay,_1st_Marquess_of_Dalhousie"] Lord Dalhousie as Governor General of the East India Company set the stage for changes
essential to a modern state. These included the consolidation and demarcation of sovereignty, the
surveillance of the population, and the education of citizens. Technological changes—among them,
railways, canals, and the telegraph—were introduced not long after their introduction in
Europe.[140][141][142][143] However, disaffection with the company also grew during this time and set off
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_Rebellion_of_1857"] Indian Rebellion of 1857. Fed by diverse resentments and perceptions, including invasive British-style
social reforms, harsh land taxes, and summary treatment of some rich landowners and princes, the rebellion
rocked many regions of northern and central India and shook the foundations of Company rule.[144][145]
Although the rebellion was suppressed by 1858, it led to the dissolution of the East India Company and the
 direct administration of India by the British government. Proclaiming a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unitary_state"] unitary state and a gradual but
limited British-style parliamentary system, the new rulers also protected princes and landed gentry as a
feudal safeguard against future unrest.[146][147] In the decades following, public life gradually emerged all
over India, leading eventually to the founding of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_National_Congress"] Indian National Congress in 1885.[148][149][150][151]
The rush of technology and the commercialisation of agriculture in the second half of the 19th century was
marked by economic setbacks and many small farmers became dependent on the whims of far-away
markets.[152] There was an increase in the number of large-scale famines,[153] and, despite the risks of
infrastructure development borne by Indian taxpayers, little industrial employment was generated for
Indians.[154] There were also salutary effects: commercial cropping, especially in the newly canalled
Punjab, led to increased food production for internal consumption.[155] The railway network provided
critical famine relief,[156] notably reduced the cost of moving goods,[156] and helped nascent Indian-owned
industry.[155] 
After World War I, in which approximately
 one million Indians served,[157] a new period
began. It was marked by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Montagu%E2%80%93Chelmsford_Reforms"] British reforms but
also [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rowlatt_act"] repressive legislation, by more strident
Indian calls for self-rule, and by the beginnings
of a  [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nonviolent"] nonviolent movement of non-co-
 operation, of which Mohandas Karamchand

Gandhi would become the leader and enduring
symbol.[158] During the 1930s, slow
legislative reform was enacted by the British;
the Indian National Congress won victories in
the resulting elections.[159] The next decade
 was beset with crises: Indian participation in
World War II, the Congress's final push for non-co-operation, and an upsurge of Muslim nationalism. All
were capped by the advent of independence in 1947, but tempered by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Partition_of_India"] partition of India into two states:
India and Pakistan.[160]
Page 8
Vital to India's self-image as an independent nation was its constitution, completed in 1950, which put in
place a secular and democratic republic.[161] It has remained a democracy with civil liberties, an active
supreme court, and a largely independent press.[162] Economic liberalisation, which began in the 1990s,
 has created a large urban middle class, transformed India into one of the world's fastest-growing
economies,[163] and increased its geopolitical clout. Indian movies, music, and spiritual teachings play an
increasing role in global culture.[162] Yet, India is also shaped by seemingly unyielding poverty, both rural
and urban;[162] by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religious_violence_in_India"] religious and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caste-related_violence_in_India"] caste-related violence;[164] by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naxalite"] Maoist-inspired Naxalite insurgencies;[165]
and by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Insurgency_in_Jammu_and_Kashmir"] separatism in Jammu and Kashmir and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Insurgency_in_Northeast_India"] in Northeast India.[166] It has unresolved territorial disputes
with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China%E2%80%93India_relations#1960s"] China[167] and with Pakistan.[167] India's sustained democratic freedoms are unique among the
world's newer nations; however, in spite of its recent economic successes, freedom from want for its
disadvantaged population remains a goal yet to be achieved.[168]
Geography
India accounts for the bulk of the Indian subcontinent, lying atop the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_Plate"] Indian tectonic plate, a part of the
 Indo-Australian Plate.[169] India's defining geological processes began 75 million years ago when the
Indian Plate, then part of the southern supercontinent Gondwana, began a north-eastward [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plate_tectonics"] drift caused by
 seafloor spreading to its south-west, and later, south and south-east.[169] Simultaneously, the vast [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tethys_Ocean"] Tethyan
 oceanic crust, to its northeast, began to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subduction"] subduct under the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurasian_Plate"] Eurasian Plate.[169] These dual processes, driven
by convection in the Earth's mantle, both created the Indian Ocean and caused the Indian [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continental_crust"] continental crust
eventually to under-thrust Eurasia and to uplift the Himalayas.[169] Immediately south of the emerging
Himalayas, plate movement created a vast crescent-shaped [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trough_(geology)"] trough that rapidly filled with river-borne
sediment[170] and now constitutes the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Gangetic_Plain"] Indo-Gangetic Plain.[171] The original Indian plate makes its first
appearance above the sediment in the ancient [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aravalli_range"] Aravalli range, which extends from the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Delhi_Ridge"] Delhi Ridge in a
southwesterly direction. To the west lies the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thar_desert"] Thar desert, the eastern spread of which is checked by the
Aravallis.[172][173][174]
The Tungabhadra, with rocky
outcrops, flows into the peninsular
 Krishna river.[175] 
The remaining Indian Plate survives as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_India"] peninsular India, the oldest
and geologically most stable part of India. It extends as far north as
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Satpura_Range"] Satpura and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vindhya_Range"] Vindhya ranges in central India. These parallel
chains run from the Arabian Sea coast in Gujarat in the west to the
coal-rich [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chota_Nagpur_Plateau"] Chota Nagpur Plateau in Jharkhand in the east.[176] To the
south, the remaining peninsular landmass, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deccan_Plateau"] Deccan Plateau, is
flanked on the west and east by coastal ranges known as the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Ghats"] Western
and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Ghats"] Eastern Ghats;[177] the plateau contains the country's oldest rock
formations, some over one billion years old. Constituted in such
fashion, India lies to the north of the equator between 6° 44′ and 35°
30′ north latitude[i] and 68° 7′ and 97° 25′ east longitude.[178]
India's coastline measures 7,517 kilometres (4,700 mi) in length; of
this distance, 5,423 kilometres (3,400 mi) belong to peninsular India
and 2,094 kilometres (1,300 mi) to the Andaman, Nicobar, and
Lakshadweep island chains.[179] According to the Indian naval
hydrographic charts, the mainland coastline consists of the following:

include the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ganges"] Ganges and the Brahmaputra, both of which drain into
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bay_of_Bengal"] Bay of Bengal.[180] Important tributaries of the Ganges include
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yamuna"] Yamuna and the Kosi; the latter's extremely low gradient, caused by long-term silt deposition, leads to
Page 9
severe floods and course changes.[181][182] Major peninsular rivers, whose steeper gradients prevent their
waters from flooding, include the Godavari, the Mahanadi, the Kaveri, and the Krishna, which also drain
into the Bay of Bengal;[183] and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Narmada_River"] Narmada and the Tapti, which drain into the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_Sea"] Arabian Sea.[184] Coastal
features include the marshy [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rann_of_Kutch"] Rann of Kutch of western India and the alluvial [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sundarbans"] Sundarbans delta of eastern
India; the latter is shared with Bangladesh.[185] India has two archipelagos: the Lakshadweep, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atoll"] coral atolls
 off India's south-western coast; and the Andaman and Nicobar Islands, a volcanic chain in the Andaman
Sea.[186]
 Indian climate is strongly influenced by the Himalayas and the Thar Desert, both of which drive the
economically and culturally pivotal summer and winter monsoons.[187] The Himalayas prevent cold
Central Asian [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Katabatic_wind"] katabatic winds from blowing in, keeping the bulk of the Indian subcontinent warmer than
most locations at similar latitudes.[188][189] The Thar Desert plays a crucial role in attracting the moisture-
laden south-west summer monsoon winds that, between June and October, provide the majority of India's
 rainfall.[187] Four major climatic groupings predominate in India: tropical wet, tropical dry, subtropical
humid, and montane.[190]
Temperatures in India have risen by 0.7 °C (1.3 °F) between 1901 and 2018.[191] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change_in_India"] Climate change in India
is often thought to be the cause. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Retreat_of_glaciers_since_1850"] retreat of Himalayan glaciers has adversely affected the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volumetric_flow_rate"] flow rate of
the major Himalayan rivers, including the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ganges"] Ganges and the Brahmaputra.[192] According to some current
projections, the number and severity of droughts in India will have markedly increased by the end of the
present century.[193]
Biodiversity
India is a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Megadiverse_country"] megadiverse country, a term employed for 17 countries
which display high [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biological_diversity"] biological diversity and contain many species
exclusively indigenous, or endemic, to them.[196] India is a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Habitat"] habitat
for 8.6% of all [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mammal"] mammal species, 13.7% of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bird"] bird species, 7.9% of
 reptile species, 6% of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amphibian"] amphibian species, 12.2% of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fish"] fish species, and
6.0% of all [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flowering_plant"] flowering plant species.[197][198] Fully a third of Indian
plant species are endemic.[199] India also contains four of the
world's 34 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biodiversity_hotspot"] biodiversity hotspots,[69] or regions that display
significant habitat loss in the presence of high endemism.[k][200]
According to official statistics, India's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forest_cover"] forest cover is 713,789 km2
(275,595 sq mi),  which is 21.71% of the country's total land
area.[70] It can be subdivided further into broad categories of
canopy density, or the proportion of the area of a forest covered by
its [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tree_canopy"] tree canopy.[201] Very dense forest, whose canopy density is
greater than 70%, occupies 3.02% of India's land area.[201][202] It
predominates in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_and_subtropical_moist_broadleaf_forest"] tropical moist forest of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andaman_Islands"] Andaman Islands,
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Ghats"] Western Ghats, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northeast_India"] Northeast India.[195] Moderately dense
forest, whose canopy density is between 40% and 70%, occupies
9.39% of India's land area.[201][202] It predominates in the
 temperate coniferous forest of the Himalayas, the moist deciduous
 sal forest of eastern India, and the dry deciduous [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Teak"] teak forest of
central and southern India.[195] Open forest, whose canopy density
is between 10% and 40%,  occupies 9.26% of India's land
area.[201][202] India has two natural zones of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deserts_and_xeric_shrublands"] thorn forest, one in 
India has the majority of the world's
wild tigers, approximately 3,000 in
2019.[194]

Gangetic plain, now turned into rich agricultural land by irrigation, its features no longer visible.[203]
Among the Indian subcontinent's notable indigenous trees are the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astringent"] astringent [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azadirachta_indica"] Azadirachta indica, or neem,
which is widely used in rural Indian [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herbal_medicine"] herbal medicine,[204] and the luxuriant [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ficus_religiosa"] Ficus religiosa, or peepul,[205]
which is displayed on the ancient seals of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohenjo-daro"] Mohenjo-daro,[206] and under which [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gautama_Buddha"] the Buddha is recorded in
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/P%C4%81li_Canon"] Pali canon to have sought enlightenment.[207]
Many Indian species have descended from those of Gondwana, the southern [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supercontinent"] supercontinent from which
India separated more than 100 million years ago.[208] India's subsequent collision with Eurasia set off a
mass exchange of species. However, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deccan_Traps"] volcanism and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_variability_and_change"] climatic changes later caused the extinction of many
endemic Indian forms.[209] Still later, mammals entered India from Asia through two [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zoogeographical"] zoogeographical
passes flanking the Himalayas.[195] This had the effect of lowering endemism among India's mammals,
which stands at 12.6%,  contrasting with 45.8% among reptiles and 55.8% among amphibians.[198]}
 Among endemics are the vulnerable[210] hooded leaf monkey[211] and the threatened[212] Beddome's
toad[212][213] of the Western Ghats.
India contains 172 IUCN-designated [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_endangered_animals_in_India"] threatened animal species, or
2.9% of endangered forms.[214] These include the endangered
 Bengal tiger and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Asian_river_dolphin"] Ganges river dolphin. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Critically_endangered"] Critically endangered
species include: the gharial, a crocodilian; the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Indian_bustard"] great Indian bustard;
and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_white-rumped_vulture"] Indian white-rumped vulture, which has become nearly
extinct by having ingested the carrion of diclofenac-treated
cattle.[215] Before they were extensively utilized for agriculture and
cleared for human settlement, the thorn forests of Punjab were
mingled at intervals with open grasslands that were grazed by large

Politics and government
Politics
 India is the world's most populous democracy.[222] A parliamentary republic with a multi-party
system,[223] it has eight recognised [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_recognised_political_parties_in_India#National"] national parties, including the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_National_Congress"] Indian National Congress and the
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bharatiya_Janata_Party"] Bharatiya Janata Party (BJP), and more than 40 regional parties.[224] The Congress is considered centre-left
in Indian [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_culture"] political culture,[225] and the BJP [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Right-wing_politics"] right-wing.[226][227][228] For most of the period between 1950
—when India first became a republic—and the late 1980s, the Congress held a majority in the parliament.
Page 11
Since then, however, it has increasingly shared the political stage
with the BJP,[229] as well as with powerful regional parties which
have often forced the creation of multi-party [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coalition_government"] coalition governments at
the centre.[230]
In the Republic of India's first three general elections, in 1951, 1957,
and 1962, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru"] Jawaharlal Nehru-led Congress won easy victories.

BJP formed a government briefly in 1996; it was followed by two
comparatively long-lasting [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Front_(India)"] United Front coalitions, which depended
on external support. In 1998, the BJP was able to form a successful

Government
India is a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federation"] federation with a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parliamentary_system"] parliamentary system governed under the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_India"] Constitution of India—the country's
 supreme legal document. It is a constitutional republic and representative democracy, in which "majority
rule is tempered by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minority_rights"] minority rights protected by law". [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federalism_in_India"] Federalism in India defines the power distribution
Page 12
between the union and the states. The Constitution of India, which
came into effect on 26 January 1950,[239] originally stated India to
be a "sovereign, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liberal_democracy"] democratic republic;" this characterisation was
 Rashtrapati Bhavan, the official 
amended in 1971 to "a sovereign, socialist, secular, democratic
republic".[240] India's form of government, traditionally described as
"quasi-federal" with a strong centre and weak states,[241] has grown
increasingly federal since the late 1990s as a result of political,
economic, and social changes.[242][243]
residence of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/President_of_India"] President of India,
was designed by British architects

comprises three [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_symbols_of_India"] National symbols[1]

 Prime Minister of India is the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Head_of_government"] head of government and
exercises most [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executive_(government)"] executive power.[248] Appointed by the

supported by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_party"] party or [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_alliance"] political alliance having a

The executive of the Indian government consists of the 
 River dolphin
 Indian peafowl
 president, the vice president, and the Union Council of  Flower [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nelumbo_nucifera"] Lotus
Ministers—with the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cabinet_(government)"] cabinet being its executive
committee—headed by the prime minister. Any minister 
Fruit [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mango"] Mango
holding a portfolio must be a member of one of the  Tree [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banyan"] Banyan
houses of parliament.[245] In the Indian parliamentary
system, the executive is subordinate to the legislature; 
River [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ganges"] Ganges
the prime minister and their council are directly responsible to the lower house of the
parliament. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_Services_of_India"] Civil servants act as permanent executives and all decisions of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executive_(government)"] executive are
implemented by them.[250]
Legislature: The legislature of India is the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bicameralism"] bicameral parliament. Operating under a
 Westminster-style parliamentary system, it comprises an upper house called the Rajya
Sabha (Council of States) and a lower house called the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lok_Sabha"] Lok Sabha (House of the
People).[251] The Rajya Sabha is a permanent body of 245 members who serve staggered
six-year terms.[252] Most are elected indirectly by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/States_and_union_territories_of_India"] state and union territorial legislatures in
numbers proportional to their state's share of the national population.[249] All but two of the
 Lok Sabha's 545 members are elected directly by popular vote; they represent single-
 member constituencies for five-year terms.[253] Two seats of parliament, reserved for Anglo-
Indian in the article 331, have been scrapped.[254][255]
 Judiciary: India has a three-tier unitary independent judiciary[256] comprising the supreme
court, headed by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chief_Justice_of_India"] Chief Justice of India, 25 high courts, and a large number of trial
 courts.[256] The supreme court has original jurisdiction over cases involving fundamental
rights and over disputes between states and the centre and has [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Appellate_jurisdiction"] appellate jurisdiction over
the high courts.[257] It has the power to both strike down union or state laws which
contravene the constitution,[258] and invalidate any government action it deems
unconstitutional.[259]
Page 13
Administrative divisions
India is a federal union comprising 28 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/States_and_union_territories_of_India"] states and 8 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Union_territory"] union territories.[16] All states, as well as the union
territories of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jammu_and_Kashmir_(union_territory)"] Jammu and Kashmir, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puducherry_(union_territory)"] Puducherry and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Delhi"] National Capital Territory of Delhi, have elected
legislatures and governments following the Westminster system of governance. The remaining five union
territories are directly ruled by the central government through appointed administrators. In 1956, under the
 States Reorganisation Act, states were reorganised on a linguistic basis.[260] There are over a quarter of a
million local government bodies at city, town, block, district and village levels.[261]

Foreign, economic and strategic relations
During the 1950s and 60s, India
 played a pivotal role in the Non-
Aligned Movement.[262] From left
to right: [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gamal_Abdel_Nasser"] Gamal Abdel Nasser of
 United Arab Republic (now Egypt),
 Josip Broz Tito of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia"] Yugoslavia and
 Jawaharlal Nehru in Belgrade,
September 1961. 
In the 1950s, India strongly supported decolonisation in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Africa"] Africa and
 Asia and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India_and_the_Non-Aligned_Movement"] played a leading role in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement"] Non-Aligned Movement.[263]
After initially cordial relations with neighbouring China, India went
to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sino-Indian_War"] war with China in 1962, and was widely thought to have been
humiliated.[264] India has had [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Pakistani_relations"] tense relations with neighbouring
Pakistan; the two nations have gone to war four times: in 1947,
1965, 1971, and 1999. Three of these wars were fought over the
 disputed territory of Kashmir, while the fourth, the 1971 war,
 followed from India's  support for the independence of
Bangladesh.[265] In the late 1980s, the Indian military twice
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_Peace_Keeping_Force"] intervened abroad at the invitation of the host country: a peace-
keeping operation in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sri_Lanka"] Sri Lanka between 1987 and 1990; and an
armed intervention to prevent a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1988_Maldives_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat"] 1988 coup d'état attempt in the
Maldives. After the 1965 war with Pakistan, India began to pursue
close military and economic [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India-Soviet_Union_relations"] ties with the Soviet Union; by the late
1960s, the Soviet Union was its largest arms supplier.[266]
 Aside from ongoing its special relationship with Russia,[267] India has wide-ranging defence relations with
 Israel and France. In recent years, it has played key roles in the South Asian Association for Regional
Cooperation and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Trade_Organization"] World Trade Organization. The nation has provided 100,000 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_Armed_Forces"] military and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_India"] police
 personnel to serve in 35 UN peacekeeping operations across four continents. It participates in the East Asia
 Summit, the G8+5, and other multilateral forums.[268] India has close economic ties with countries in South
America,[269] Asia, and Africa; it pursues a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Look_East_policy_(India)"] "Look East" policy that seeks to strengthen partnerships with
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Association_of_Southeast_Asian_Nations"] ASEAN nations, Japan, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India%E2%80%93South_Korea_relations"] South Korea that revolve around many issues, but especially those
involving economic investment and regional security.[270][271]
China's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/596_(nuclear_test)"] nuclear test of 1964, as well as its repeated threats to
intervene in support of Pakistan in the 1965 war, convinced India to
 develop nuclear weapons.[273] India conducted its first nuclear
weapons test in 1974 and carried out [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pokhran-II"] additional underground testing
in 1998. Despite criticism and military sanctions, India has signed
 neither the Comprehensive Nuclear-Test-Ban Treaty nor the Nuclear
Non-Proliferation Treaty, considering both to be flawed and
discriminatory.[274] India maintains a "[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/No_first_use"] no first use" nuclear policy
 and is developing a nuclear triad capability as a part of its "Minimum
 Credible Deterrence" doctrine.[275][276] It is developing a ballistic
missile defence shield and, a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HAL_AMCA"] fifth-generation fighter jet.[277][278]
Other indigenous military projects involve the design and
 implementation of Vikrant-class aircraft carriers and Arihant-class
nuclear submarines.[279] 
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_Air_Force"] Indian Air Force contingent
 marching at the 221st Bastille Day
military parade in Paris, on 14 July
2009. The parade at which India
was the foreign guest was led by
the India's oldest regiment, the
 Maratha Light Infantry, founded in
1768.[272]
Since the end of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War"] Cold War, India has increased its economic,
strategic, and military co-operation with the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India%E2%80%93United_States_relations"] United States and the
 European Union.[280] In 2008, a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S.%E2%80%93India_Civil_Nuclear_Agreement"] civilian nuclear agreement was signed between India and the United
States. Although India possessed nuclear weapons at the time and was not a party to the Nuclear Non-
 Proliferation Treaty, it received waivers from the International Atomic Energy Agency and the Nuclear
Page 15
 Suppliers Group, ending earlier restrictions on India's nuclear technology and commerce. As a
consequence, India became the sixth de facto nuclear weapons state.[281] India subsequently signed co-
 operation agreements involving civilian nuclear energy with Russia,[282] France,[283] the United
Kingdom,[284] and Canada.[285] 
The President of India is the supreme commander of the nation's
armed forces; with 1.45 million active troops, they compose the
 world's second-largest military. It comprises the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_Army"] Indian Army, the
 Indian Navy, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_Air_Force"] Indian Air Force, and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_Coast_Guard"] Indian Coast Guard.[286]
The official Indian [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_military_expenditures"] defence budget for 2011 was US$36.03 billion,
or 1.83% of GDP.[287] Defence expenditure was pegged at
US$70.12 billion for fiscal year 2022–23 and, increased 9.8% than
Prime Minister [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Narendra_Modi"] Narendra Modi of
India (left, background) in talks
with President [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Enrique_Pe%C3%B1a_Nieto"] Enrique Peña Nieto
of Mexico during a visit to Mexico,
2016 
previous fiscal year.[288][289] India is the world's second largest arms
importer; between 2016 and 2020, it accounted for 9.5% of the total
global arms imports.[290] Much of the military expenditure was
focused on defence against Pakistan and countering growing
 Chinese influence in the Indian Ocean.[291] In May 2017, the Indian
Space Research Organisation launched the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Asia_Satellite"] South Asia Satellite, a
gift from India to its neighbouring [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SAARC"] SAARC countries.[292] In
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/S-400_Triumf"] October 2018, India signed a US$5.43 billion (over ₹400 billion) agreement with Russia to procure four S-
400 Triumf surface-to-air missile defence systems, Russia's most advanced long-range [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Missile_defence"] missile defence
system.[293]
Economy
According to the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund"] International Monetary Fund (IMF), the Indian economy in 2021 was nominally worth
$3.04 trillion; it is the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)"] sixth-largest economy by market exchange rates, and is around $10.219 trillion, the
 third-largest by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity"] purchasing power parity (PPP).[297] With its average annual GDP growth rate of 5.8% over
 the past two decades, and reaching 6.1% during 2011–2012,[298] India is one of the world's fastest-growing
economies.[299] However, the country ranks 139th in the world in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)_per_capita"] nominal GDP per capita and 118th in
 GDP per capita at PPP.[300] Until 1991, all Indian governments followed [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protectionism"] protectionist policies that were
influenced by socialist economics. Widespread [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Licence_Raj"] state intervention and regulation largely walled the economy
 off from the outside world. An acute balance of payments crisis in 1991 forced the nation to liberalise its
economy;[301] since then it has moved slowly towards a free-market system[302][303] by emphasising both
foreign trade and direct investment inflows.[304] India has been a member of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Trade_Organization"] World Trade Organization
since 1 January 1995.[305]
The 522-million-worker [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Labour_in_India"] Indian labour force is the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_labour_force"] world's second-largest, as of 2017.[286] The service
sector makes up 55.6% of GDP, the industrial sector 26.3% and the agricultural sector 18.1%. India's
 foreign exchange remittances of US$87 billion in 2021, highest in the world, were contributed to its
economy by 32 million Indians working in foreign countries.[306] Major agricultural products include: rice,
wheat, oilseed, cotton, jute, tea, sugarcane, and potatoes.[16] Major industries include: textiles,
telecommunications, chemicals, pharmaceuticals, biotechnology, food processing, steel, transport
equipment, cement, mining, petroleum, machinery, and software.[16] In 2006, the share of external trade in
India's GDP stood at 24%, up from 6% in 1985.[302] In 2008, India's share of world trade was 1.68%;[307]
In 2011, India was the world's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_imports"] tenth-largest importer and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_exports"] nineteenth-largest exporter.[308] Major exports
include: petroleum products, textile goods, jewellery, software, engineering goods, chemicals, and
manufactured leather goods.[16] Major imports include: crude oil, machinery, gems, fertiliser, and
Page 16
chemicals.[16] Between 2001 and 2011, the contribution of
petrochemical and engineering goods to total exports grew from
14% to 42%.[309] India was the world's second largest textile
exporter after [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China"] China in the 2013 calendar year.[310]
Averaging an economic growth rate of 7.5% for several years prior
to 2007,[302] India has more than doubled its hourly wage rates
during the first decade of the 21st century.[311] Some 431 million
Indians have left poverty since 1985; India's middle classes are
projected to number around 580 million by 2030.[312] Though
ranking 51st in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_Competitiveness_Report"] global competitiveness, as of 2010, India ranks
17th in financial market sophistication, 24th in the banking sector,
44th in business sophistication, and 39th in innovation, ahead of
several advanced economies.[313] With seven of the world's top 15
information technology outsourcing companies based in India, as
of 2009, the country is viewed as the second-most favourable
outsourcing destination after the United States.[314] India was
ranked 46th in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_Innovation_Index"] Global Innovation Index in 2021, it has
increased its ranking considerably since 2015, where it was
81st.[315][316][317][318] India's  consumer market, the world's
 eleventh-largest, is expected to become fifth-largest by 2030.[312] 
A farmer in northwestern [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karnataka"] Karnataka
ploughs his field with a tractor even
as another in a field beyond does the
same with a pair of oxen. In 2019,
43% of India's total workforce was
employed in agriculture.[294]
Driven by growth, India's nominal [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GDP_per_capita"] GDP per capita increased
steadily from US$308 in 1991, when economic liberalisation
began, to US$1,380 in 2010, to an estimated US$1,730 in 2016. It
is expected to grow to US$2,313 by 2022.[21] However, it has
remained lower than those of other Asian developing countries
such as Indonesia, Malaysia, Philippines, Sri Lanka, and Thailand,
and is expected to remain so in the near future. 
India is the world's largest producer
of milk, with the largest population of
cattle. In 2018, nearly 80% of India's
milk was sourced from small farms
with herd size between one and two,
the milk harvested by hand
milking.[296]
According to a 2011 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/PricewaterhouseCoopers"] PricewaterhouseCoopers (PwC) report,
India's GDP at purchasing power parity could overtake that of the
United States by 2045.[320] During the next four decades, Indian
GDP is expected to grow at an annualised average of 8%, making
it potentially the world's fastest-growing major economy until
2050.[320] The report highlights key growth factors: a young and
rapidly growing working-age population; growth in the
manufacturing sector because of rising education and engineering
skill levels; and sustained growth of the consumer market driven by
a rapidly growing middle-class.[320] The World Bank cautions that,
for India to achieve its economic potential, it must continue to
focus on public sector reform, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transport_in_India"] transport infrastructure, agricultural
and rural development, removal of labour regulations, education,
 energy security, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Healthcare_in_India"] public health and nutrition.[321] 
Women tend to a recently planted
rice field in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Junagadh"] Junagadh district in
Gujarat. 55% of India's female
workforce was employed in
agriculture in 2019.[295]
According to the Worldwide Cost of Living Report 2017 released by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economist_Intelligence_Unit"] Economist Intelligence Unit
(EIU) which was created by comparing more than 400 individual prices across 160 products and services,
four of the cheapest cities were in India: [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bangalore"] Bangalore (3rd), [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mumbai"] Mumbai (5th), [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chennai"] Chennai (5th) and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Delhi"] New Delhi
(8th).[322]
Industries
Page 17
A panorama of Bangalore, the centre of India's software development economy. In
the 1980s, when the first [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multinational_corporation"] multinational corporations began to set up centres in
India, they chose Bangalore because of the large pool of skilled graduates in the
area, in turn due to the many science and engineering colleges in the surrounding
region.[319]
India's [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Telecommunications_in_India"] telecommunication industry is the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_mobile_network_operators"] second-largest in the world
with over 1.2 billion subscribers. It contributes 6.5% to India's
GDP.[323] After the third quarter of 2017, India surpassed the US to
become the second largest smartphone market in the world after
China.[324]
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automotive_industry_in_India"] Indian automotive industry, the world's second-fastest growing,
increased domestic sales by 26% during 2009–2010,[325] and
exports by 36% during 2008–2009.[326] At the end of 2011, the
 Indian IT industry employed 2.8 million professionals, generated
revenues close to US$100 billion equalling 7.5% of Indian GDP, and
contributed 26% of India's merchandise exports.[327] 
A tea garden in Sikkim. India, the
world's second largest-producer of
tea, is a nation of one billion tea
drinkers, who consume 70% of
India's tea output.
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pharmaceutical_industry_in_India"] pharmaceutical industry in India emerged as a global player. As
of 2021, with 3000 pharmaceutical companies and 10,500 manufacturing units India is the world's third-
largest pharmaceutical producer, largest producer of generic medicines and supply up to 50%—60% of
global vaccines demand, these all contribute up to US$24.44 billions in exports and India's local
pharmacutical market is estimated up to US$42 billion.[328][329] India is among the top 12 biotech
destinations in the world.[330][331] The Indian biotech industry grew by 15.1% in 2012–2013, increasing its
revenues from ₹204.4 billion ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_rupee"] Indian rupees) to ₹235.24 billion (US$3.94 billion at June 2013 exchange
rates).[332]
Energy
 India's capacity to generate electrical power is 300 gigawatts, of which 42 gigawatts is renewable.[333] The
country's usage of coal is a major cause of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change_in_India#Greenhouse_gas_emissions"] greenhouse gas emissions by India but its [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Renewable_energy_in_India"] renewable energy is
competing strongly.[334] India emits about 7% of global greenhouse gas emissions. This equates to about
 2.5 tons of carbon dioxide per person per year, which is half the world average.[335][336] Increasing access
to electricity and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clean_cooking"] clean cooking with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liquefied_petroleum_gas"] liquefied petroleum gas have been priorities for [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Energy_in_India"] energy in India.[337]
Socio-economic challenges
Despite economic growth during recent decades, India continues to face socio-economic challenges. In
2006, India contained the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poverty_in_India"] largest number of people living below the World Bank's international poverty line
of US$1.25 per day.[339] The proportion decreased from 60% in 1981 to 42% in 2005.[340] Under the
World Bank's later revised poverty line, it was 21% in 2011.[l][342] 30.7% of India's children under the age
Page 18
Health workers about to begin
another day of immunisation
against infectious diseases in
2006. Eight years later, and three
years after India's last case of
 polio, the World Health
Organization declared India to be
polio-free.[338] 
 of five are underweight.[343] According to a Food and Agriculture
Organization report in 2015, 15% of the population is
undernourished.[344][345] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mid-Day_Meal_Scheme"] Mid-Day Meal Scheme attempts to
lower these rates.[346]
A 2018 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walk_Free_Foundation"] Walk Free Foundation report estimated that nearly 8 million
people in India were living in different forms of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modern_slavery"] modern slavery,
such as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bonded_labour"] bonded labour, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Child_labour"] child labour, human trafficking, and forced
begging, among others.[347] According to the 2011 census, there
were 10.1 million child labourers in the country, a decline of
2.6 million from 12.6 million in 2001.[348]
Since 1991, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Indian_states_by_GDP"] economic inequality between India's  states has
consistently grown: the per-capita [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Net_domestic_product"] net state domestic product of the
richest states in 2007 was 3.2 times that of the poorest.[349]
 Corruption in India is perceived to have decreased. According to the
 Corruption Perceptions Index, India ranked 78th out of 180 countries
in 2018 with a score of 41 out of 100, an improvement from 85th in
2014.[350][351]
Demographics, languages, and religion
 With 1,210,193,422 residents reported in the 2011 provisional census
report,[352] India is the world's second-most populous country. Its
population grew by 17.64% from 2001 to 2011,[353] compared to 21.54%
growth in the previous decade (1991–2001).[353] The human sex ratio,
according to the 2011 census, is 940 females per 1,000 males.[352] The
median age was 28.7 as of 2020.[286] The first post-colonial census,
conducted in 1951, counted 361 million people.[354] Medical advances
made in the last 50 years as well as increased agricultural productivity
brought about by the "[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_Revolution_in_India"] Green Revolution" have caused India's population to
grow rapidly.[355] 
India by language
The average life expectancy in India is at 70 years—71.5 years for women,
68.7 years for men.[286] There are around 93 physicians per 100,000
people.[356] Migration from rural to urban areas has been an important 
The language families of
South Asia
dynamic in India's recent history. The number of people living in urban
areas grew by 31.2% between 1991 and 2001.[357] Yet, in 2001, over 70% still lived in rural
areas.[358][359] The level of urbanisation increased further from 27.81% in the 2001 Census to 31.16% in
the 2011 Census. The slowing down of the overall population growth rate was due to the sharp decline in
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_million-plus_urban_agglomerations_in_India"] the growth rate in rural areas since 1991.[360] According to the 2011 census, there are 53 million-plus urban
agglomerations in India; among them Mumbai, Delhi, Kolkata, Chennai, Bangalore, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyderabad"] Hyderabad and
Ahmedabad, in decreasing order by population.[361] The literacy rate in 2011 was 74.04%: 65.46% among
females and 82.14% among males.[362] The rural-urban literacy gap, which was 21.2 percentage points in
2001, dropped to 16.1 percentage points in 2011. The improvement in the rural literacy rate is twice that of
urban areas.[360] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kerala"] Kerala is the most literate state with 93.91% literacy; while [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bihar"] Bihar the least with
63.82%.[362]

India is home to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Languages_of_India"] two major language families: [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Aryan_languages"] Indo-Aryan (spoken
by about 74% of the population) and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dravidian_languages"] Dravidian (spoken by 24% of
the population). Other languages spoken in India come from the
 Austroasiatic and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sino-Tibetan_languages"] Sino-Tibetan language families. India has no
national language.[363] Hindi, with the largest number of speakers, is
the official language of the government.[364][365] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_language"] English is used
extensively in business and administration and has the status of a
"subsidiary official language";[6] it is important in education,

Culture
Indian cultural history spans more than 4,500 years.[368] During the
 Vedic period (c. 1700 BCE – c. 500 BCE), the foundations of Hindu
philosophy, mythology, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindu_theology"] theology and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindu_texts"] literature were laid, and many
beliefs and practices which still exist today, such as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dharma"] dhárma, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karma"] kárma,
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yoga"] yóga,  and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moksha"] mokṣa,  were established.[74] India is notable for its
 religious diversity, with Hinduism, Buddhism, Sikhism, Islam,
Christianity, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jainism"] Jainism among the nation's major religions.[369]
The predominant religion, Hinduism, has been shaped by various
historical schools of thought, including those of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Upanishads"] Upanishads,[370]
 the Yoga Sutras,  the Bhakti movement,[369] and by Buddhist
philosophy.[371] 
 A Sikh pilgrim at the Harmandir
Sahib, or Golden Temple, in
Amritsar, Punjab
Visual art
India has a very ancient tradition of art, which has exchanged many influences with the rest of Eurasia,
especially in the first millennium, when [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddhist_art"] Buddhist art spread with Indian religions to Central, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Asia"] East and
 South-East Asia, the last also greatly influenced by Hindu art.[372] Thousands of seals from the Indus
Valley Civilization of the third millennium BCE have been found, usually carved with animals, but a few
with human figures. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%22Pashupati%22_seal"] "Pashupati" seal, excavated in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohenjo-daro"] Mohenjo-daro, Pakistan, in 1928–29, is the best
known.[373][374] After this there is a long period with virtually nothing surviving.[374][375] Almost all
surviving ancient Indian art thereafter is in various forms of religious [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_sculpture"] sculpture in durable materials, or
coins. There was probably originally far more in wood, which is lost. In north India [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mauryan_art"] Mauryan art is the first
imperial movement.[376][377][378] In the first millennium CE, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddhist_art"] Buddhist art spread with Indian religions to
Central, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Asia"] East and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South-East_Asia"] South-East Asia, the last also greatly influenced by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindu_art"] Hindu art.[379] Over the following
centuries a distinctly Indian style of sculpting the human figure developed, with less interest in articulating
precise anatomy than [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greek_sculpture"] ancient Greek sculpture but showing smoothly-flowing forms expressing prana
("breath" or life-force).[380][381] This is often complicated by the need to give figures multiple arms or
heads, or represent different genders on the left and right of figures, as with the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ardhanarishvara"] Ardhanarishvara form of
Shiva and Parvati.[382][383]
Page 20
Most of the earliest large sculpture is Buddhist, either excavated from Buddhist [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stupa"] stupas such as Sanchi,
 Sarnath and Amaravati,[384] or is rock-cut [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Relief"] reliefs at sites such as Ajanta, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karla_Caves"] Karla and Ellora. Hindu and Jain
sites appear rather later.[385][386] In spite of this complex mixture of religious traditions, generally, the
prevailing artistic style at any time and place has been shared by the major religious groups, and sculptors
probably usually served all communities.[387] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gupta_art"] Gupta art, at its peak c. 300 CE – c. 500 CE, is often
regarded as a classical period whose influence lingered for many centuries after; it saw a new dominance of
Hindu sculpture, as at the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elephanta_Caves"] Elephanta Caves.[388][389] Across the north, this became rather stiff and
formulaic after c. 800 CE, though rich with finely carved detail in the surrounds of statues.[390] But in the
 South, under the Pallava and Chola dynasties, sculpture in both stone and bronze had a sustained period of
great achievement; the large bronzes with Shiva as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nataraja"] Nataraja have become an iconic symbol of
India.[391][392]
 Ancient painting has only survived at a few sites, of which the crowded scenes of court life in the Ajanta
Caves are by far the most important, but it was evidently highly developed, and is mentioned as a courtly
accomplishment in Gupta times.[393][394] Painted manuscripts of religious texts survive from Eastern India
about the 10th century onwards, most of the earliest being Buddhist and later Jain. No doubt the style of
these was used in larger paintings.[395] The Persian-derived [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deccan_painting"] Deccan painting, starting just before the
 Mughal miniature, between them give the first large body of secular painting, with an emphasis on portraits,
and the recording of princely pleasures and wars.[396][397] The style spread to Hindu courts, especially
 among the Rajputs, and developed a variety of styles, with the smaller courts often the most innovative,
with figures such as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nih%C3%A2l_Chand"] Nihâl Chand and Nainsukh.[398][399] As a market developed among European
residents, it was supplied by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Company_painting"] Company painting by Indian artists with considerable Western
influence.[400][401] In the 19th century, cheap [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kalighat_painting"] Kalighat paintings of gods and everyday life, done on paper,
were urban [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Folk_art"] folk art from Calcutta, which later saw the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bengal_School_of_Art"] Bengal School of Art, reflecting the art colleges
founded by the British, the first movement in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modern_Indian_painting"] modern Indian painting.[402][403]
