Architecture 
Much of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Architecture_of_India"] Indian architecture, including the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taj_Mahal"] Taj Mahal, other
 works of Indo-Islamic Mughal architecture, and South Indian
architecture, blends ancient local traditions with imported
styles.[404] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_vernacular_architecture"] Vernacular architecture is also regional in its
flavours. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vastu_shastra"] Vastu shastra,  literally "science of construction" or
"architecture" and ascribed to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mamuni_Mayan"] Mamuni Mayan,[405] explores
how the laws of nature affect human dwellings;[406] it employs
precise geometry and directional alignments to reflect perceived
 The Taj Mahal from across the Yamuna cosmic constructs.[407] As applied in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindu_temple_architecture"] Hindu temple architecture,
river showing two outlying red  it is influenced by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shilpa_Shastras"] Shilpa Shastras, a series of foundational
sandstone buildings, a mosque on the
right (west) and a jawab (response)
thought to have been built for
architectural balance. 
texts whose basic mythological form is the Vastu-Purusha
mandala, a square that embodied the "absolute".[408] The Taj
Mahal, built in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agra"] Agra between 1631 and 1648 by orders of
 Mughal emperor [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shah_Jahan"] Shah Jahan in memory of his wife, has been
described in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_List"] UNESCO World Heritage List as "the jewel of
Muslim art in India and one of the universally admired
masterpieces of the world's heritage".[409] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Saracenic_Revival_architecture"] Indo-Saracenic Revival architecture, developed by the British in
the late 19th century, drew on [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Islamic_architecture"] Indo-Islamic architecture.[410]
Literature
The earliest literature in India, composed between 1500 BCE and 1200 CE, was in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanskrit"] Sanskrit
language.[411] Major works of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanskrit_literature"] Sanskrit literature include the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rigveda"] Rigveda (c. 1500 BCE – c. 1200 BCE), the
epics: [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahabharata"] Mahābhārata ( c. 400 BCE – c. 400 CE) and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ramayana"] Ramayana (  c. 300 BCE and later);
Abhijñānaśākuntalam ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Recognition_of_%C5%9Aakuntal%C4%81"] The Recognition of Śakuntalā, and other dramas of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/K%C4%81lid%C4%81sa"] Kālidāsa ( c. 5th century CE)
and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanskrit_Classical_poetry"] Mahākāvya poetry.[412][413][414] In [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tamil_literature"] Tamil literature, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sangam_literature"] Sangam literature (c. 600 BCE – c. 300 BCE)
consisting of 2,381 poems, composed by 473 poets, is the earliest work.[415][416][417][418] From the 14th to
the 18th centuries, India's literary traditions went through a period of drastic change because of the
emergence of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bhakti_movement"] devotional poets like Kabīr, Tulsīdās, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guru_Nanak"] Guru Nānak. This period was characterised by a
varied and wide spectrum of thought and expression; as a consequence, medieval Indian literary works
differed significantly from classical traditions.[419] In the 19th century, Indian writers took a new interest in
social questions and psychological descriptions. In the 20th century, Indian literature was influenced by the
 works of the Bengali poet, author and philosopher [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rabindranath_Tagore"] Rabindranath Tagore,[420] who was a recipient of the
 Nobel Prize in Literature.
Performing arts and media
 Indian music ranges over various traditions and regional styles. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_classical_music"] Classical music encompasses two genres
and their various folk offshoots: the northern [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindustani_classical_music"] Hindustani and southern [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carnatic_music"] Carnatic schools.[421] Regionalised
popular forms include [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Filmi"] filmi and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_folk_music"] folk music; the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syncretism"] syncretic tradition of the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baul"] bauls is a well-known form of the
latter. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dance_in_India"] Indian dance also features diverse folk and classical forms. Among the better-known [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Indian_folk_dances"] folk dances are:
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bhangra_(dance)"] bhangra of Punjab, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bihu_dance"] bihu of Assam, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jhumair"] Jhumair and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chhau_dance"] chhau of Jharkhand, Odisha and West Bengal,
 garba and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dandiya_Raas"] dandiya of Gujarat, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghoomar"] ghoomar of Rajasthan, and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lavani"] lavani of Maharashtra. Eight dance forms,
many with narrative forms and mythological elements, have been accorded [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Classical_Indian_dance"] classical dance status by India's
 National Academy of Music, Dance, and Drama. These are: [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bharata_Natyam"] bharatanatyam of the state of Tamil Nadu,
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kathak"] kathak of Uttar Pradesh, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kathakali"] kathakali and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohiniyattam"] mohiniyattam of Kerala, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuchipudi"] kuchipudi of Andhra Pradesh, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manipuri_dance"] manipuri of
Manipur, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Odissi"] odissi of Odisha, and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sattriya"] sattriya of Assam.[422]
Page 23
 Theatre in India melds music, dance, and improvised or written
dialogue.[423] Often based on Hindu mythology, but also borrowing from
medieval romances or social and political events, Indian theatre includes:
the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bhavai"] bhavai of Gujarat, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jatra_(Bengal)"] jatra of West Bengal, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nautanki"] nautanki and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ramlila"] ramlila of
North India, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tamasha"] tamasha of Maharashtra, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Burrakatha"] burrakatha of Andhra Pradesh and
Telangana, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terukkuttu"] terukkuttu of Tamil Nadu, and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yakshagana"] yakshagana of
 Karnataka.[424] India has a theatre training institute the National School of
Drama (NSD) that is situated at [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Delhi"] New Delhi It is an autonomous
organisation under the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_Culture_(India)"] Ministry of Culture, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_of_India"] Government of India.[425]The
 Indian film industry produces the world's most-watched cinema.[426]
Established regional cinematic traditions exist in the Assamese, Bengali,
Bhojpuri, Hindi, Kannada, Malayalam, Punjabi, Gujarati, Marathi, Odia,
Tamil, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Telugu_cinema"] Telugu languages.[427] The Hindi language film industry
(Bollywood) is the largest sector representing 43% of box office revenue,
followed by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cinema_of_South_India"] South Indian Telugu and Tamil film industries which
represent 36% combined.[428] 
 India's National Academy of
Performance Arts has
recognised eight Indian
dance styles to be
Television broadcasting began in India in 1959 as a state-run medium of
communication and expanded slowly for more than two decades.[429][430] 
classical. One such is
 Kuchipudi shown here.
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doordarshan"] state monopoly on television broadcast ended in the 1990s. Since then,
satellite channels have increasingly shaped the popular culture of Indian
society.[431] Today, television is the most penetrative media in India; industry estimates indicate that as of
2012 there are over 554 million TV consumers, 462 million with satellite or cable connections compared to
other forms of mass media such as the press (350 million), radio (156 million) or internet (37 million).[432]
Society 
Traditional Indian society is sometimes defined by social hierarchy.
The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caste_system_in_India"] Indian caste system embodies much of the social stratification
and many of the social restrictions found on the Indian subcontinent.
Social classes are defined by thousands of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endogamous"] endogamous hereditary
groups, often termed as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J%C4%81ti"] jātis,  or "castes".[433] India declared
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Untouchability"] untouchability to be illegal in 1947 and has since enacted other anti-
discriminatory laws and social welfare initiatives.
Muslims offer [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salah"] namaz at a mosque
in Srinagar, Jammu and Kashmir. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Family_values"] Family values are important in the Indian tradition, and multi-
generational [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patrilineal"] patrilineal [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joint_family"] joint families have been the norm in India,
though [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_family"] nuclear families are becoming common in urban areas.[434]
An overwhelming majority of Indians, with their consent, have [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arranged_marriage_in_the_Indian_subcontinent"] their marriages arranged by their parents or
other family elders.[435] Marriage is thought to be for life,[435] and the divorce rate is extremely low,[436]
with less than one in a thousand marriages ending in divorce.[437] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Child_marriage"] Child marriages are common, especially
 in rural areas; many women wed before reaching 18, which is their legal marriageable age.[438] Female
 infanticide in India, and lately female foeticide, have created skewed gender ratios; the number of missing
women in the country quadrupled from 15 million to 63 million in the 50-year period ending in 2014, faster
than the population growth during the same period, and constituting 20 percent of India's female
electorate.[439] Accord to an Indian government study, an additional 21 million girls are unwanted and do
not receive adequate care.[440] Despite a government ban on sex-selective foeticide, the practice remains
commonplace in India, the result of a preference for boys in a patriarchal society.[441] The payment of
dowry, although illegal, remains widespread across class lines.[442] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dowry_deaths"] Deaths resulting from dowry, mostly
from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bride_burning"] bride burning, are on the rise, despite stringent anti-dowry laws.[443]
Page 24
 Many Indian festivals are religious in origin. The best known include: Diwali, Ganesh Chaturthi, Thai
Pongal, Holi, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Durga_Puja"] Durga Puja, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eid_ul-Fitr"] Eid ul-Fitr, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bakr-Id"] Bakr-Id, Christmas, and Vaisakhi.[444][445]
Education
In the 2011 census, about 73% of the population was literate, with
81% for men and 65% for women. This compares to 1981 when
the respective rates were 41%, 53% and 29%. In 1951 the rates
were 18%, 27% and 9%. In 1921 the rates 7%, 12% and 2%. In
1891 they were 5%, 9% and 1%,[446][447] According to Latika
Chaudhary, in 1911 there were under three primary schools for
every ten villages. Statistically, more caste and religious diversity
reduced private spending. Primary schools taught literacy, so local
diversity limited its growth.[448]
The education system of India is the world's second-largest.[449]
India has over 900 universities, 40,000 colleges[450] and 1.5
million schools.[451] In India's  higher education system, a
significant number of seats are reserved under [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reservation_in_India"] affirmative action
policies for the historically disadvantaged. In recent decades India's
improved education system is often cited as one of the main
contributors to its [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_development_in_India"] economic development.[452][453] 
Children awaiting school lunch in
Rayka (also Raika), a village in rural
Gujarat. The salutation [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jai_Bhim"] Jai Bhim
written on the blackboard honours
the jurist, social reformer, and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dalit"] Dalit
leader [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/B._R._Ambedkar"] B. R. Ambedkar.
Clothing
From ancient times until the advent of the
modern, the most widely worn traditional dress
in India was draped.[454] For women it took
the form of a sari, a single piece of cloth many
yards long.[454] The sari was traditionally
wrapped around the lower body and the
shoulder.[454] In its modern form, it is
combined with an underskirt, or Indian
petticoat, and tucked in the waist band for
more secure fastening. It is also commonly
worn with an Indian blouse, or choli, which 
Women in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sari"] sari at an adult literacy
class in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tamil_Nadu"] Tamil Nadu
serves as the primary upper-body garment, the
sari's end—passing over the shoulder—serving
to cover the midriff and obscure the upper
body's contours.[454] For men, a similar but
shorter length of cloth, the dhoti, has served as a lower-body garment.[455] 
A man in [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dhoti"] dhoti
and wearing a
woollen shawl, in
 Varanasi
 The use of stitched clothes became widespread after Muslim rule was established at first by the Delhi
sultanate (ca 1300 CE) and then continued by the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mughal_Empire"] Mughal Empire (ca 1525 CE).[456] Among the garments
introduced during this time and still commonly worn are: the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shalwar"] shalwars and pyjamas, both styles of trousers,
and the tunics [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurta"] kurta and kameez.[456] In southern India, the traditional draped garments were to see much
longer continuous use.[456]
Page 25
Shalwars are atypically wide at the waist but narrow to a cuffed bottom.
They are held up by a drawstring, which causes them to become pleated
around the waist.[457] The pants can be wide and baggy, or they can be cut
quite narrow, on the bias, in which case they are called churidars. When
they are ordinarily wide at the waist and their bottoms are hemmed but not
cuffed, they are called pyjamas. The kameez is a long shirt or tunic,[458] its
side seams left open below the waist-line.[459] The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurta"] kurta is traditionally
collarless and made of cotton or silk; it is worn plain or with embroidered
decoration, such as chikan; and typically falls to either just above or just
below the wearer's knees.[460]
Women (from left to right) in
 churidars and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kameez"] kameez (with
back to the camera), jeans
and sweater, and pink
 Shalwar kameez; 
In the last 50 years, fashions have changed a great deal in India.
Increasingly, in urban northern India, the sari is no longer the apparel of
everyday wear, though they remain popular on formal occasions.[461] The
traditional shalwar kameez is rarely worn by younger urban women, who
favour churidars or jeans.[461] In white-collar office settings, ubiquitous air
conditioning allows men to wear sports jackets year-round.[461] For
weddings and formal occasions, men in the middle- and upper classes often
wear bandgala, or short [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nehru_jackets"] Nehru jackets, with pants, with the groom and his [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Groomsmen"] groomsmen sporting [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sherwani"] sherwanis
and churidars.[461] The dhoti, once the universal garment of Hindu males, the wearing of which in the
homespun and handwoven [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khadi"] khadi allowed Gandhi to bring Indian nationalism to the millions,[462]is seldom
seen in the cities.[461]
Cuisine
The foundation of a typical Indian meal is a cereal cooked in a plain
fashion and complemented with flavourful savoury dishes.[463] The cooked
cereal could be steamed rice; chapati, a thin unleavened bread made from
wheat flour, or occasionally cornmeal, and griddle-cooked dry;[464] the idli,
a steamed breakfast cake, or dosa, a griddled pancake, both leavened and
made from a batter of rice- and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vigna_mungo"] gram meal.[465] The savoury dishes might
include lentils, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pulses"] pulses and vegetables commonly spiced with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ginger_root"] ginger and
garlic, but also with a combination of spices that may include coriander,
cumin, turmeric, cinnamon, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cardamon"] cardamon and others as informed by culinary
conventions.[463] They might also include poultry, fish, or meat dishes. In
some instances, the ingredients might be mixed during the process of
cooking.[466] 
South Indian vegetarian
thali, or platter
A platter, or thali, used for eating usually has a central place reserved for
the cooked cereal, and peripheral ones for the flavourful accompaniments,
which are often served in small bowls. The cereal and its accompaniments
are eaten simultaneously rather than a piecemeal manner. This is 
 Railway mutton curry from
 Odisha
accomplished by mixing—for example of rice and lentils—or folding,
wrapping, scooping or dipping—such as chapati and cooked vegetables or lentils.[463]
India has distinctive vegetarian cuisines, each a feature of the geographical and cultural histories of its
adherents.[468] The appearance of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahimsa"] ahimsa, or the avoidance of violence toward all forms of life in many
religious orders early in Indian history, especially [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Upanishads"] Upanishadic Hinduism, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddhism"] Buddhism and Jainism, is
thought to have contributed to the predominance of vegetarianism among a large segment of India's Hindu
population, especially in southern India, Gujarat, the Hindi-speaking belt of north-central India, as well as
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thali"]
Page 26
among Jains.[468] Although meat is eaten widely in India, the
proportional consumption of meat in the overall diet is low.[469] Unlike
China, which has increased its per capita meat consumption substantially
in its years of increased economic growth, in India the strong dietary
traditions have contributed to dairy, rather than meat, becoming the
preferred form of animal protein consumption.[470]
The most significant import of cooking techniques into India during the
last millennium occurred during the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mughal_Empire"] Mughal Empire. Dishes such as the
pilaf,[471] developed in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abbasid_caliphate"] Abbasid caliphate,[472] and cooking
techniques such as the marinating of meat in yogurt, spread into northern
India from regions to its northwest.[473] To the simple yogurt marinade of
Persia, onions, garlic, almonds, and spices began to be added in
India.[473] Rice was partially cooked and layered alternately with the
sauteed meat, the pot sealed tightly, and slow cooked according to another
Persian cooking technique, to produce what has today become the Indian
biryani,[473] a feature of festive dining in many parts of India.[474] In the
 A tandoor chef in the Turkman
Gate, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Delhi"] Old Delhi, makes
Khameeri [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roti"] roti (a Muslim-
 influenced style of leavened
bread).[467] 
food served in Indian restaurants worldwide the diversity of Indian food
has been partially concealed by the dominance of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Punjabi_cuisine"] Punjabi cuisine. The
popularity of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tandoori_chicken"] tandoori chicken—cooked in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tandoor"] tandoor oven, which had
traditionally been used for baking bread in the rural Punjab and the Delhi
 region, especially among Muslims, but which is originally from Central
Asia—dates to the 1950s, and was caused in large part by an
entrepreneurial response among people from the Punjab who had been
displaced by the 1947 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Partition_of_India"] partition of India.[468]
Sports and recreation
Several traditional indigenous sports such as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kabaddi"] kabaddi,  [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kho_kho"] kho kho,
 pehlwani and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gilli-danda"] gilli-danda,  and also [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_martial_arts"] martial arts, such as
 Kalarippayattu and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marma_adi"] marma adi remain popular. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chess"] Chess is commonly
held to have [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_chess#India"] originated in India as [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chaturanga"] chaturaṅga;[476] There has been a
rise in the number of Indian grandmasters.[477] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viswanathan_Anand"] Viswanathan Anand
became the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Chess_Championship_2007"] undisputed Chess World Champion in 2007 and held the
status until 2013.[478] [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parcheesi"] Parcheesi is derived from [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pachisi"] Pachisi another
traditional Indian pastime, which in early modern times was played Girls play [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hopscotch"] hopscotch in Jaora,
on a giant marble court by [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mughal_Empire"] Mughal emperor [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Akbar_the_Great"] Akbar the Great.[479]  Madhya Pradesh. Hopscotch has
been commonly played by girls in
 Cricket is the most popular sport in India.[480] Major domestic rural India.[475]
competitions include the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_Premier_League"] Indian Premier League, which is the most-
watched cricket league in the world and ranks sixth among all sports
leagues.[481] Other professional leagues include the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_Super_League"] Indian Super League (football) and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pro_Kabaddi_League"] pro Kabaddi
league.[482][483][484]
India has won two [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/One_Day_International"] ODI [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cricket_World_Cup"] Cricket world cups, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1983_Cricket_World_Cup"] 1983 edition and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2011_Cricket_World_Cup"] 2011 edition and has eight field
 hockey gold medals in the summer olympics[485]The improved results garnered by the Indian Davis Cup
team and other [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Category:Indian_tennis_players"] Indian tennis players in the early 2010s have made tennis increasingly popular in the
country.[486] India has a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Category:Indian_sport_shooters"] comparatively strong presence in shooting sports, and has won several medals at
the Olympics, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISSF_World_Shooting_Championships"] World Shooting Championships, and the Commonwealth Games.[487][488] Other sports
in which Indians have succeeded internationally include [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Badminton"] badminton[489] ([URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saina_Nehwal"] Saina Nehwal and [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/P._V._Sindhu"] P. V. Sindhu

are two of the top-ranked female
badminton players in the world),
boxing,[490] and wrestling.[491]

Bengal, Goa, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tamil_Nadu"] Tamil Nadu,
 Kerala, and the north-eastern

states.[492]India has hosted or

[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010_Commonwealth_Games"] Trophy; the 2009 World Badminton Championships; the 2010 Hockey World Cup; the 2010
Commonwealth Games; and the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017_FIFA_U-17_World_Cup"] 2017 FIFA U-17 World Cup. Major international sporting events held
annually in India include the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maharashtra_Open"] Maharashtra Open, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mumbai_Marathon"] Mumbai Marathon, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Delhi_Half_Marathon"] Delhi Half Marathon, and the

three out of four tournaments to date.[494]

Notes
a. "[...] Jana Gana Mana is the National Anthem of India, subject to such alterations in the
words as the Government may authorise as occasion arises; and the song Vande Mataram,
which has played a historic part in the struggle for Indian freedom, shall be honoured equally
with Jana Gana Mana and shall have equal status with it."[5]
b. According to [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Part_XVII_of_the_Constitution_of_India"] Part XVII of the Constitution of India, [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standard_Hindi"] Hindi in the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Devanagari"] Devanagari script is the
 official language of the Union, along with [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_English"] English as an additional official language.[1][6][7]
 States and union territories can have a different official language of their own other than
Hindi or English.
c. Different sources give widely differing figures, primarily based on how the terms "language"
and "dialect" are defined and grouped. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnologue"] Ethnologue lists 461 tongues for India (out of 6,912
worldwide), 447 of which are living, while 14 are extinct.[13][14]
d. "The country's exact size is subject to debate because some borders are disputed. The
Indian government lists the total area as 3,287,260 km2 (1,269,220 sq mi) and the total land
area as 3,060,500 km2 (1,181,700 sq mi); the United Nations lists the total area as
3,287,263 km2 (1,269,219 sq mi) and total land area as 2,973,190 km2
(1,147,960 sq mi)."[16]
e. See [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Date_and_time_notation_in_India"] Date and time notation in India.
f. The [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_of_India"] Government of India also regards [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghanistan"] Afghanistan as a bordering country, as it considers all
of [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kashmir"] Kashmir to be part of India. However, this is disputed, and the region bordering
 Afghanistan is administered by Pakistan. Source: "Ministry of Home Affairs (Department of
Border Management)" (https://web.archive.org/web/20150317182910/https://mha.nic.in/site
 s/upload_files/mha/files/BMIntro-1011.pdf) (PDF). Archived from the original (https://mha.nic.
in/sites/upload_files/mha/files/BMIntro-1011.pdf) (PDF) on 17 March 2015. Retrieved
1 September 2008.
[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bangalore"]
Page 28
g. "A Chinese pilgrim also recorded evidence of the caste system as he could observe it.
According to this evidence the treatment meted out to untouchables such as the Chandalas
was very similar to that which they experienced in later periods. This would contradict
assertions that this rigid form of the caste system emerged in India only as a reaction to the
Islamic conquest."[41]
h. "Shah Jahan eventually sent her body 800 km (500 mi) to Agra for burial in the Rauza-i
Munauwara ("Illuminated Tomb") – a personal tribute and a stone manifestation of his
imperial power. This tomb has been celebrated globally as the Taj Mahal."[49]
i. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jammu_and_Kashmir_(union_territory)"] The northernmost point under Indian control is the disputed Siachen Glacier in Jammu and
Kashmir; however, the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_of_India"] Government of India regards the entire region of the former princely
state of Jammu and Kashmir, including the [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gilgit-Baltistan"] Gilgit-Baltistan administered by Pakistan, to be
its territory. It therefore assigns the latitude 37° 6′ to its northernmost point.
j. A forest cover is moderately dense if between 40% and 70% of its area is covered by its tree
canopy.
k. A biodiversity hotspot is a [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biogeography"] biogeographical region which has more than 1,500 [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vascular_plant"] vascular plant
species, but less than 30% of its primary habitat.[200]
l. In 2015, the World Bank raised its international poverty line to $1.90 per day.[341]
m. Besides specific religions, the last two categories in the 2011 Census were "Other religions
and persuasions" (0.65%) and "Religion not stated" (0.23%).

28. Dyson 2018, p. 1 [URL: "https://books.google.com/books?id=3TRtDwAAQBAJ&pg=PA1"] (https://books.google.com/books?id=3TRtDwAAQBAJ&pg=PA1), "Modern
human beings—Homo sapiens—originated in Africa. Then, intermittently, sometime
between 60,000 and 80,000 years ago, tiny groups of them began to enter the north-west of
the Indian subcontinent. It seems likely that initially they came by way of the coast. ... it is
virtually certain that there were Homo sapiens in the subcontinent 55,000 years ago, even
though the earliest fossils that have been found of them date to only about 30,000 years
before the present."
29. Fisher 2018, p. 23 [URL: "https://books.google.com/books?id=kZVuDwAAQBAJ&pg=PA23"] (https://books.google.com/books?id=kZVuDwAAQBAJ&pg=PA23),
"Scholars estimate that the first successful expansion of the Homo sapiens range beyond
Africa and across the Arabian Peninsula occurred from as early as 80,000 years ago to as
late as 40,000 years ago, although there may have been prior unsuccessful emigrations.
Some of their descendants extended the human range ever further in each generation,
spreading into each habitable land they encountered. One human channel was along the
warm and productive coastal lands of the Persian Gulf and northern Indian Ocean.
Eventually, various bands entered India between 75,000 years ago and 35,000 years ago."

33. [URL: "https://books.google.com/books?id=SKBxa-MNqA8C&pg=PA68"] (a) Witzel, Michael (2008). "Vedas and Upanisads" (https://books.google.com/books?id=SK
Bxa-MNqA8C&pg=PA68). In Gavin Flood (ed.). The Blackwell Companion to Hinduism.
 John Wiley & Sons. pp. 68–70. ISBN 978-[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-470-99868-7"] 0-470-99868-7. "It is known from internal evidence
that the Vedic texts were orally composed in northern India, at first in the Greater Punjab and
later on also in more eastern areas, including northern Bihar, between ca. 1500 BCE and ca.
500–400 BCE. The oldest text, the Rgveda, must have been more or less contemporary with
the Mitanni texts of northern Syria/Iraq (1450–1350 BCE); ... The Vedic texts were orally
composed and transmitted, without the use of script, in an unbroken line of transmission from
teacher to student that was formalized early on. This ensured an impeccable textual
transmission superior to the classical texts of other cultures; it is in fact something of a tape-
recording of ca. 1500–500 BCE. Not just the actual words, but even the long-lost musical
(tonal) accent (as in old Greek or in Japanese) has been preserved up to the present. (pp.
68–69) ... The RV text was composed before the introduction and massive use of iron, that is
before ca. 1200–1000 BCE. (p. 70)"
 (b) Doniger, Wendy (3 February 2014), On Hinduism (https://books.google.com/books?id=fU
naAgAAQBAJ&pg=PR18), [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxford_University_Press"] Oxford University Press, pp. xviii, 10, ISBN 978-[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-19-936009-3"] 0-19-936009-3,
"A Chronology of Hinduism: ca. 1500-1000 BCE Rig Veda; ca. 1200-900 BCE Yajur Veda,
Sama Veda and Atharva Veda (p. xviii); Hindu texts began with the Rig Veda ('Knowledge of
Verses'), composed in northwest India around 1500 BCE (p. 10)"
(c) Ludden 2014, p. 19 [URL: "https://books.google.com/books?id=pBq9DwAAQBAJ&pg=PA19"] (https://books.google.com/books?id=pBq9DwAAQBAJ&pg=PA19),
"In Punjab, a dry region with grasslands watered by five rivers (hence ‘panch’ and ‘ab’)
draining the western Himalayas, one prehistoric culture left no material remains, but some of
its ritual texts were preserved orally over the millennia. The culture is called Aryan, and
evidence in its texts indicates that it spread slowly south-east, following the course of the
Yamuna and Ganga Rivers. Its elite called itself Arya (pure) and distinguished themselves
sharply from others. Aryans led kin groups organized as nomadic horse-herding tribes. Their
ritual texts are called Vedas, composed in Sanskrit. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vedic_Sanskrit"] Vedic Sanskrit is recorded only in hymns
that were part of Vedic rituals to Aryan gods. To be Aryan apparently meant to belong to the
elite among pastoral tribes. Texts that record Aryan culture are not precisely datable, but they
seem to begin around 1200 BCE with four collections of Vedic hymns (Rg, Sama, Yajur, and
Artharva)."
 (d) Dyson 2018, pp. 14–15 (https://books.google.com/books?id=3TRtDwAAQBAJ&pg=PA1
4), "Although the collapse of the Indus valley civilization is no longer believed to have been
due to an ‘Aryan invasion’ it is widely thought that, at roughly the same time, or perhaps a
few centuries later, new Indo-Aryan-speaking people and influences began to enter the
subcontinent from the north-west. Detailed evidence is lacking. Nevertheless, a predecessor
of the language that would eventually be called Sanskrit was probably introduced into the
north-west sometime between 3,900 and 3,000 years ago. This language was related to one
then spoken in eastern Iran; and both of these languages belonged to the Indo-European
language family. ... It seems likely that various small-scale migrations were involved in the
gradual introduction of the predecessor language and associated cultural characteristics.
However, there may not have been a tight relationship between movements of people on the
one hand, and changes in language and culture on the other. Moreover, the process
whereby a dynamic new force gradually arose—a people with a distinct ideology who
eventually seem to have referred to themselves as ‘Arya’—was certainly two-way. That is, it
involved a blending of new features which came from outside with other features—probably
including some surviving Harappan influences—that were already present. Anyhow, it would
be quite a few centuries before Sanskrit was written down. And the hymns and stories of the
Arya people—especially the Vedas and the later Mahabharata and Ramayana epics—are
poor guides as to historical events. Of course, the emerging Arya were to have a huge
impact on the history of the subcontinent. Nevertheless, little is known about their early
presence."; 
(e) Robb 2011, pp. 46– [URL: "https://books.google.com/books?id=GQ-2VH1LO_EC&pg=PA46"] (https://books.google.com/books?id=GQ-2VH1LO_EC&pg=PA46),
Page 33
"The expansion of Aryan culture is supposed to have begun around 1500 BCE. It should not
be thought that this Aryan emergence (though it implies some migration) necessarily meant
either a sudden invasion of new peoples, or a complete break with earlier traditions. It
comprises a set of cultural ideas and practices, upheld by a Sanskrit-speaking elite, or
Aryans. The features of this society are recorded in the Vedas."
34. [URL: "https://books.google.com/books?id=1LTRDwAAQBAJ"] (a) Jamison, Stephanie; Brereton, Joel (2020), The Rigveda (https://books.google.com/book
s?id=1LTRDwAAQBAJ), [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oxford_University_Press"] Oxford University Press, pp. 2, 4, ISBN 978-[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-19-063339-4"] 0-19-063339-4, "The
RgVeda is one of the four Vedas, which together constitute the oldest texts in Sanskrit and
the earliest evidence for what will become Hinduism. (p. 2) Although Vedic religion is very
different in many regards from what is known as Classical Hinduism, the seeds are there.
Gods like Visnu and Siva (under the name Rudra), who will become so dominant later, are
already present in the Rgveda, though in roles both lesser than and different from those they
will later play, and the principal Rgvedic gods like Indra remain in later Hinduism, though in
diminished capacity (p. 4).";
 (b) Flood, Gavin (20 August 2020), "Introduction" (https://books.google.com/books?id=4yT3
DwAAQBAJ&pg=PA4), in Gavin Flood (ed.), The Oxford History of Hinduism: Hindu

the term ‘Hinduism to meaningfully denote a range and history of practice characterized by a
number of features, particularly reference to Vedic textual and sacrificial origins, belonging to
endogamous social units (jati/varna), participating in practices that involve making an
offering to a deity and receiving a blessing (puja), and a first-level cultural polytheism
(although many Hindus adhere to a second-level monotheism in which many gods are
regarded as emanations or manifestations of the one, supreme being).";
 (c) Michaels, Axel (2017). Patrick Olivelle, Donald R. Davis (ed.). The Oxford History of
Hinduism: Hindu Law: A New History of Dharmaśāstra (https://books.google.com/books?id=
 QAJCDwAAQBAJ&pg=PA86). Oxford: Oxford University Press. pp. 86–97. ISBN 978-0-19-
100709-5. "Almost all traditional Hindu families observe until today at least three samskaras
(initiation, marriage, and death ritual). Most other rituals have lost their popularity, are
combined with other rites of passage, or are drastically shortened. Although samskaras vary
from region to region, from class (varna) to class, and from caste to caste, their core
elements remain the same owing to the common source, the Veda, and a common priestly
tradition preserved by the Brahmin priests. (p 86)"

56. Fisher 2018, pp. 173–174: "The partition of South Asia that produced India and West and
East Pakistan resulted from years of bitter negotiations and recriminations ... The departing
British also decreed that the hundreds of princes, who ruled one-third of the subcontinent
and a quarter of its population, became legally independent, their status to be settled later.
Geographical location, personal and popular sentiment, and substantial pressure and
incentives from the new governments led almost all princes eventually to merge their
domains into either Pakistan or India. ... Each new government asserted its exclusive
sovereignty within its borders, realigning all territories, animals, plants, minerals, and all
other natural and human-made resources as either Pakistani or Indian property, to be used
for its national development... Simultaneously, the central civil and military services and
judiciary split roughly along religious 'communal' lines, even as they divided movable
government assets according to a negotiated formula: 22.7 percent for Pakistan and 77.3
percent for India."
57. Chatterji, Joya; Washbrook, David (2013), "Introduction: Concepts and Questions", in
Chatterji, Joya; Washbrook, David (eds.), Routledge Handbook of the South Asian Diaspora,
London and New York: Routledge, ISBN 978-[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-415-48010-9"] 0-415-48010-9, " Joya [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joya_Chatterji"] Chatterji describes how
the partition of the British Indian empire into the new nation states of India and Pakistan
produced new diaspora on a vast, and hitherto unprecedented, scale, but hints that the
sheer magnitude of refugee movements in South Asia after 1947 must be understood in the
context of pre-existing migratory flows within the partitioned regions (see also Chatterji
2013). She also demonstrates that the new national states of India and Pakistan were
quickly drawn into trying to stem this migration. As they put into place laws designed to
restrict the return of partition emigrants, this produced new dilemmas for both new nations in
their treatment of ‘overseas Indians’; and many of them lost their right to return to their places
of origin in the subcontinent, and also their claims to full citizenship in host countries."
58. [URL: "https://books.google.com/books?id=utKmPQAACAAJ"] Talbot, Ian; Singh, Gurharpal (2009), The Partition of India (https://books.google.com/books?
 id=utKmPQAACAAJ), Cambridge University Press, ISBN 978-0-521-85661-4, archived (http

British divided and quit India in August 1947, they not only partitioned the subcontinent with
the emergence of the two nations of India and Pakistan but also the provinces of Punjab and

59. [URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yasmin_Khan"] Khan, Yasmin (2017) [2007], The Great Partition: The Making of India and Pakistan (2 ed.),
New Haven and London: Yale University Press, p. 1, ISBN 978-[URL: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-300-23032-1"] 0-300-23032-1, " South
Asians learned that the British Indian empire would be partitioned on 3 June 1947. They
heard about it on the radio, from relations and friends, by reading newspapers and, later,
through government pamphlets. Among a population of almost four hundred million, where
the vast majority live in the countryside, ploughing the land as landless peasants or
sharecroppers, it is hardly surprising that many thousands, perhaps hundreds of thousands,
did not hear the new for many weeks afterwards. For some, the butchery and forced
relocation of the summer months of 1947 may hve been the first that they knew about the
creation of the two new states rising from the fragmentary and terminally weakened British
empire in India"

203. Tritsch 2001, p. 14India has two natural zones of thorn forest, one in the rain shadow area of
the Deccan Plateau east of the Western Ghats, and the other in the western part of the Indo-
Gangetic plain. Growth is limited only by moisture availability in these areas, so with
irrigation the fertile alluvial soil of Punjab and Haryana has been turned into India's prime
agricultural area. Much of the thorn forest covering the plains probably had savannah-like
features now no longer visible.

216. Tritsch 2001, p. 17Before it was so heavily settled and intensively exploited, the Punjab was
dominated by thorn forest interspersed by rolling grasslands which were grazed on by
millions of Blackbuck, accompanied by their dominant predator, the Cheetah. Always keen
hunters, the Moghul princes kept tame cheetahs which were used to chase and bring down
the Blackbuck. Today the Cheetah is extinct in India and the severely endangered
Blackbuck no longer exists in the Punjab.

more likely to stop having children than families where a girl is born”.

465. [URL: "https://books.google.com/books?id=jLFmiervaqMC&pg=PA180"] Tamang, J. P.; Fleet, G. H. (2009), "Yeasts Diversity in Fermented Foods and Beverages" (htt
ps://books.google.com/books?id=jLFmiervaqMC&pg=PA180), in Satyanarayana, T.; Kunze,
 G. (eds.), Yeast Biotechnology: Diversity and Applications, Springer, p. 180, ISBN 978-1-
4020-8292-4, "Idli is an acid-leavened and steamed cake made by bacterial fermentation of
a thick batter made from coarsely ground rice and dehulled black gram. Idli cakes are soft,
moist and spongy, have desirable sour flavour, and is eaten as breakfast in South India.
Dosa batter is very similar to idli batter, except that both the rice and black gram are finely
grounded. The batter is thinner than that of idli and is fried as a thin, crisp pancake and
eaten directly in South India."
466. [URL: "https://books.google.com/books?id=WGpECgAAQBAJ&pg=PA70"] Jhala, Angma Day (2015), Royal Patronage, Power and Aesthetics in Princely India (https://
 books.google.com/books?id=WGpECgAAQBAJ&pg=PA70), Routledge, p. 70, ISBN 978-1-
317-31657-2, "With the ascent of the Mughal Empire in sixteenth-century India, Turkic,
Persian and Afghan traditions of dress, 'architecture and cuisine' were adopted by non-
Muslim indigenous elites in South Asia. In this manner, Central Asian cooking merged with
older traditions within the subcontinent, to create such signature dishes as biryani (a fusion
of the Persian pilau and the spice-laden dishes of Hindustan), and the Kashmiri meat stew
of Rogan Josh. It not only generated new dishes and entire cuisines, but also fostered novel
modes of eating. Such newer trends included the consumption of Persian condiments,
which relied heavily on almonds, pastries and quince jams, alongside Indian achars made
from sweet limes, green vegetables and curds as side relishes during Mughlai meals."
